### SubsetAttrInsert

- Category: Attribute Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:create, category:attribute, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:attribute, object:dimension, object:subset, value:enum, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_ti_func_subsetattrinsert.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

SubsetAttrInsert creates a new attribute for subsets on your TM1® server. The function creates a string, numeric, or alias attribute.

This function is valid in TM1 TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
SubsetAttrInsert( Dimension, PrevAttrName, NewAttrName, AttrType);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Dimension | string | The name of the dimension whose subsets are being updated. |
| PrevAttrName | string | The attribute that precedes the attribute you are creating. If there is no previous attribute or
you want the new attribute to be the first attribute for subsets, leave this argument empty. |
| NewAttrName | string | The name you want to assign to the new subset attribute. |
| AttrType | enum | The type of attribute. There are three possible values for the AttrType argument: N - Creates a numeric attribute. S - Creates a string attribute. A - Creates an alias attribute. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| Dimension | The name of the dimension whose subsets are being updated. |
| PrevAttrName | The attribute that precedes the attribute you are creating. If there is no previous attribute or
you want the new attribute to be the first attribute for subsets, leave this argument empty. |
| NewAttrName | The name you want to assign to the new subset attribute. |
| AttrType | The type of attribute. There are three possible values for the AttrType argument: N - Creates a numeric attribute. S - Creates a string attribute. A - Creates an alias attribute. |

#### Example Notes

This example creates the Description string attribute for subsets in the Model dimension. Because
there is no PrevAttrName parameter, this attribute is inserted as the first attribute for subsets on
your TM1 server.

#### Examples

```ti
SubsetAttrInsert('Model', '', 'Description', 'S');
```

#### Notes

- If you update an existing subset attribute, you must first delete the existing attribute using
the function SubsetAttrDelete. You can then use SubsetAttrInsert to recreate the attribute with your
desired changes.  If you attempt to update an existing attribute without first deleting it, the
insert fails without a warning or error. The existing attribute remains unchanged; it is neither
updated nor overwritten.

#### Example Notes

subset from the Plan_Business_Unit dimension.

#### Examples

```ti
SubsetATTRS('Plan_Business_Unit', 'Sales', 'Manager');
```

### SubsetATTRSL

- Category: Attribute Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:update, category:attribute, feature:locale, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:attribute, object:dimension, object:subset, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_ti_func_subsetattrsl.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

SubsetATTRSL returns an attribute's string value for a specified subset with respect to a
given locale.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
SubsetATTRSL(DimName, SubName, AttrName, [LangLocaleCode]);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | A valid dimension name. |
| SubName | string | The name of a subset in a dimension. |
| AttrName | string | The attribute for which you want to retrieve a value. This argument must be a valid attribute of
the dimension. |
| LangLocaleCode | string | This optional parameter specifies the language locale code for which you want to return a value. Valid LangLocaleCode values correspond to the international language codes listed in the
}Cultures control dimension. When the LangLocaleCode is not specified or is omitted, the user's current locale is used as the
LangLocaleCode argument. If an attribute value does not exist for the LangLocaleCode, the value for an associated parent
LangLocaleCode is returned. If an attribute value does not exist for an associated parent
LangLocaleCode, the base attribute value is returned. For example if the LangLocaleCode is fr-CA , the function returns the attribute
value for the fr-CA (French-Canada) locale if available. If the attribute value for fr-CA is not available, the function attempts to return the attribute value for the
parent fr (French) locale. If the attribute value for fr is not
available, the base attribute value is returned |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | A valid dimension name. |
| SubName | The name of a subset in a dimension. |
| AttrName | The attribute for which you want to retrieve a value. This argument must be a valid attribute of
the dimension. |
| LangLocaleCode | This optional parameter specifies the language locale code for which you want to return a value. Valid LangLocaleCode values correspond to the international language codes listed in the
}Cultures control dimension. When the LangLocaleCode is not specified or is omitted, the user's current locale is used as the
LangLocaleCode argument. If an attribute value does not exist for the LangLocaleCode, the value for an associated parent
LangLocaleCode is returned. If an attribute value does not exist for an associated parent
LangLocaleCode, the base attribute value is returned. For example if the LangLocaleCode is fr-CA , the function returns the attribute
value for the fr-CA (French-Canada) locale if available. If the attribute value for fr-CA is not available, the function attempts to return the attribute value for the
parent fr (French) locale. If the attribute value for fr is not
available, the base attribute value is returned |

#### Example Notes

In this example, the function returns the string value of the Manager attribute of the Sales
subset for the French locale.

#### Examples

```ti
SubsetATTRSL('Plan_Business_Unit', 'Sales', 'Manager', 'fr');
```

### TurboIntegrator Functions

- Category: Attribute Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19

- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/c_tm1turbointegratorfunctions_n70006.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

TurboIntegrator lets you manipulate
Planning Analytics
data and metadata when you define a
process.

This is accomplished through the use of functions in the Prolog, Metadata, Data, and Epilog
sub-tabs within the Advanced tab of the TurboIntegrator window. These sub-tabs include generated
statements based on settings and options you select when defining a TurboIntegrator process. Any
functions you create must appear after the generated statements. For details on creating processes
with TurboIntegrator, see the
TurboIntegrator
documentation.

- Valid in: unknown

### ViewAttrDelete

- Category: Attribute Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions

### ViewAttrInsert

- Category: Attribute Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:create, category:attribute, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:attribute, object:cube, object:view, value:enum, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_ti_func_viewattrinsert.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ViewAttrInsert creates a new attribute for views of a specific cube on your TM1® server. The function can create a string, numeric, or alias
attribute.

This function is valid in TM1 TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
ViewAttrInsert( CubeName, PrevAttrName, NewAttrName, AttrType);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| CubeName | string | The parent cube for which you want to insert a view attribute. |
| PrevAttrName | string | The attribute that precedes the attribute you are creating. If there is no previous attribute or
you want the new attribute to be the first attribute for views, leave this argument empty. |
| NewAttrName | string | The name you want to assign to the new view attribute. |
| AttrType | enum | The type of attribute. There are three possible values for the AttrType argument: N - Creates a numeric attribute. S - Creates a string attribute. A - Creates an alias attribute. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| CubeName | The parent cube for which you want to insert a view attribute. |
| PrevAttrName | The attribute that precedes the attribute you are creating. If there is no previous attribute or
you want the new attribute to be the first attribute for views, leave this argument empty. |
| NewAttrName | The name you want to assign to the new view attribute. |
| AttrType | The type of attribute. There are three possible values for the AttrType argument: N - Creates a numeric attribute. S - Creates a string attribute. A - Creates an alias attribute. |

#### Example Notes

This example creates the Description string attribute for views of the Sales cube. This attribute
is inserted after the Owner attribute.

#### Examples

```ti
ViewAttrInsert('Sales', 'Owner', 'Description', 'S');
```

#### Notes

- If you update an existing view attribute, you must first delete the existing attribute using
the function ViewAttrDelete. You can then use ViewAttrInsert to recreate the attribute with your
desired changes. If you attempt to update an existing attribute without first deleting it, the
insert fails without a warning or error. The existing attribute remains unchanged; it is neither
updated nor overwritten.

}Cultures control dimension. When the LangLocaleCode is not specified or is omitted, the user's current locale is used as the

}Cultures control dimension. When the LangLocaleCode is not specified or is omitted, the user's current locale is used as the
LangLocaleCode argument. If an attribute value does not exist for the LangLocaleCode, the value for an associated parent
LangLocaleCode is returned. If an attribute value does not exist for an associated parent
LangLocaleCode, the base attribute value is returned. For example if the LangLocaleCode is fr-CA , the function returns the attribute
value for the fr-CA (French-Canada) locale if available. If the attribute value for fr-CA is not available, the function attempts to return the attribute value for the
parent fr (French) locale. If the attribute value for fr is not

### ViewAttrPutN

- Category: Attribute Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:update, category:attribute, feature:locale, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:attribute, object:cube, object:view, value:number, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_ti_func_viewattrputn.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ViewAttrPutN assigns a value to a numeric view attribute.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
ViewAttrPutN(NumericValue, CubeName, ViewName, AttrName, [LangLocaleCode] );
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| NumericValue | number | The value you want to assign to a view attribute. |
| CubeName | string | The parent cube of the view for which you want to assign an attribute value. |
| ViewName | string | The view for which you want to assign an attribute value. |
| AttrName | string | The attribute whose value you want to assign. |
| LangLocaleCode | string | This optional parameter specifies the language locale code to which the NumericValue applies. Valid LangLocaleCode values correspond to the ISO 639-1 international language codes listed in
the }Cultures control dimension. When the LangLocaleCode is not specified or is omitted, the base attribute value is updated. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| NumericValue | The value you want to assign to a view attribute. |
| CubeName | The parent cube of the view for which you want to assign an attribute value. |
| ViewName | The view for which you want to assign an attribute value. |
| AttrName | The attribute whose value you want to assign. |
| LangLocaleCode | This optional parameter specifies the language locale code to which the NumericValue applies. Valid LangLocaleCode values correspond to the ISO 639-1 international language codes listed in
the }Cultures control dimension. When the LangLocaleCode is not specified or is omitted, the base attribute value is updated. |

#### Example Notes

This example assigns the value 8222001 to the Category_Code attribute of the Product view of the
Sales cube, for the French language locale code.

#### Examples

```ti
ViewAttrPutN(8222001, 'Sales', 'Product', 'Category_Code','fr');
```

## Attribute rules functions

### ATTRN

- Category: Attribute rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:read, object:attribute, object:dimension, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_attrn.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ATTRN returns a numeric attribute for a specified element of a dimension or a dimension
hierarchy.

This function is valid in both rules and processes.

- Valid in: unknown

#### Syntax Variants

```ti
ATTRN(dimension, element, attribute)
```

```ti
V1 = CELLGETN('PNLCube', 'fred',
'argentina','Sales','Jan');
IF(V1 = 454);ASCIIOUTPUT
('bug.txt', 'if logic not working
 properly');
ENDIF;
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| dimension | string | A valid dimension name. |
| element | string | An element of the dimension or a hierarchy/element pair. If specifying a hierarchy/element pair, you must use this syntax: 'hierarchy_name:element_name' . Note that the hierarchy name and element name are
enclosed in one set of single quotes. |
| attribute | string | The attribute for which you want to retrieve a value. This argument must be a valid attribute of
the element. Note: : When this function is used in a conditional statement (IF), the statement is the
portion containing the condition, not the entire conditional block. After a minor error, execution
continues with the next statement. TurboIntegrator processing has no knowledge that it was in a
conditional once the minor error is processed, so the next statement is the next line, not the line
after the endif. To avoid this situation, use variables for any operation that could encounter a minor error and
then use the variables in the conditional statement. For example: V1 = CELLGETN('PNLCube', 'fred',
'argentina','Sales','Jan');
IF(V1 = 454);ASCIIOUTPUT
('bug.txt', 'if logic not working
 properly');
ENDIF; |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| dimension | A valid dimension name. |
| element | An element of the dimension or a hierarchy/element pair. If specifying a hierarchy/element pair, you must use this syntax: 'hierarchy_name:element_name' . Note that the hierarchy name and element name are
enclosed in one set of single quotes. |
| attribute | The attribute for which you want to retrieve a value. This argument must be a valid attribute of
the element. Note: : When this function is used in a conditional statement (IF), the statement is the
portion containing the condition, not the entire conditional block. After a minor error, execution
continues with the next statement. TurboIntegrator processing has no knowledge that it was in a
conditional once the minor error is processed, so the next statement is the next line, not the line
after the endif. To avoid this situation, use variables for any operation that could encounter a minor error and
then use the variables in the conditional statement. For example: V1 = CELLGETN('PNLCube', 'fred',
'argentina','Sales','Jan');
IF(V1 = 454);ASCIIOUTPUT
('bug.txt', 'if logic not working
 properly');
ENDIF; |

#### Example Notes

In this example, the function returns the numeric value of the Engine Size attribute of the L
Series 1.8L Sedan element in the New Offerings hierarchy of the Model dimension.

#### Examples

```ti
ATTRN('Model', 'New offerings:L Series 1.8L Sedan', 'Engine Size')
```

#### Notes

- : When this function is used in a conditional statement (IF), the statement is the
portion containing the condition, not the entire conditional block. After a minor error, execution
continues with the next statement. TurboIntegrator processing has no knowledge that it was in a
conditional once the minor error is processed, so the next statement is the next line, not the line
after the endif.

- Category: Attribute rules functions


#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| CubeName | string | A valid cube name. |
| AttrName | string | The attribute for which you want to retrieve a value. This argument must be a valid attribute of
the cube. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| CubeName | A valid cube name. |
| AttrName | The attribute for which you want to retrieve a value. This argument must be a valid attribute of
the cube. |

#### Example Notes

In this example, the function returns the string value of the Owner attribute of the Product
cube.

#### Examples

```ti
CubeATTRS('Product', 'Owner');
```

### ElementAttrN

- Category: Attribute rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:read, feature:rules-and-ti, object:attribute, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_elementattrn.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ElementAttrN returns a numeric attribute for a specified element of a
dimension.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax Variants

```ti
ElementAttrN(dimension, hierarchy, element, attribute)
```

```ti
V1 = CELLGETN('PNLCube', 'fred',
'argentina','Sales','Jan');
IF(V1 = 454);ASCIIOUTPUT
('bug.txt', 'if logic not working
 properly');
ENDIF;
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| dimension | string | A valid dimension name. |
| hierarchy | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| element | string | An element of the dimension. |
| attribute | string | The attribute for which you want to retrieve a value. This argument must be a valid attribute of
the element. Note: : When this function is used in a conditional statement (IF), the statement is the
portion containing the condition, not the entire conditional block. After a minor error, execution
continues with the next statement. TI processing has no knowledge that it was in a conditional once
the minor error is processed, so the next statement is the next line, not the line after the endif. To avoid this situation, use variables for any operation that could encounter a minor error and
then use the variables in the conditional statement. For example: V1 = CELLGETN('PNLCube', 'fred',
'argentina','Sales','Jan');
IF(V1 = 454);ASCIIOUTPUT
('bug.txt', 'if logic not working
 properly');
ENDIF; |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| dimension | A valid dimension name. |
| hierarchy | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| element | An element of the dimension. |
| attribute | The attribute for which you want to retrieve a value. This argument must be a valid attribute of
the element. Note: : When this function is used in a conditional statement (IF), the statement is the
portion containing the condition, not the entire conditional block. After a minor error, execution
continues with the next statement. TI processing has no knowledge that it was in a conditional once
the minor error is processed, so the next statement is the next line, not the line after the endif. To avoid this situation, use variables for any operation that could encounter a minor error and
then use the variables in the conditional statement. For example: V1 = CELLGETN('PNLCube', 'fred',
'argentina','Sales','Jan');
IF(V1 = 454);ASCIIOUTPUT
('bug.txt', 'if logic not working
 properly');
ENDIF; |

#### Example Notes

In this example, the function returns the numeric value of the Engine Size attribute of the L
Series 1.8L Sedan element in the Automobile hierarchy of the Model dimension.

#### Examples

```ti
ElementAttrN('Model', 'Automobile', 'L Series 1.8L Sedan', 'Engine Size')
```

#### Notes

- : When this function is used in a conditional statement (IF), the statement is the
portion containing the condition, not the entire conditional block. After a minor error, execution
continues with the next statement. TI processing has no knowledge that it was in a conditional once
the minor error is processed, so the next statement is the next line, not the line after the endif.

## Chore Management TurboIntegrator Functions

### ChoreError

- Category: Chore Management TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:chore, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:chore
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ti_func_choreerror.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ChoreError causes the immediate termination of a chore. It can be called from any process
within a chore. The ChoreError TurboIntegrator function causes an immediate
termination of a single chore. Chores terminated with this function are flagged with an error
status.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
ChoreError;
```

#### Arguments

None.

### ChoreQuit

- Category: Chore Management TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:chore, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:chore
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_chorequit.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ChoreQuit causes the immediate termination of a chore. It can be called from any process
within a chore. The current chore is terminated with an error status, and a message
is written to the server log file indicating that ChoreQuit was called to terminate the
chore.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
ChoreQuit;
```

#### Arguments

None.

### ChoreRollback

- Category: Chore Management TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:chore, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:chore
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_chorerollback.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ChoreRollback initiates a chore rollback. When used inside a
TurboIntegrator process, this function throws out all pending edits and cancels further processing.
An error message appears in the tm1server.log and tm1processorerrorXXX.log files.

When used in a single-commit mode chore,
ChoreRollback
throws out all
pending edits from all previous processes and chore execution stops with an error code. When used in
a multi-commit mode chore,
ChoreRollback
throws out all pending edits from
the current processes and chore execution stops with an error code. Changes that have already been
committed cannot be rolled back.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
ChoreRollback;
```

#### Arguments

None.

### TurboIntegrator Functions

- Category: Chore Management TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:chore
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/c_tm1turbointegratorfunctions_n70006.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

TurboIntegrator lets you manipulate
Planning Analytics
data and metadata when you define a
process.

This is accomplished through the use of functions in the Prolog, Metadata, Data, and Epilog
sub-tabs within the Advanced tab of the TurboIntegrator window. These sub-tabs include generated
statements based on settings and options you select when defining a TurboIntegrator process. Any
functions you create must appear after the generated statements. For details on creating processes
with TurboIntegrator, see the
TurboIntegrator
documentation.

- Valid in: unknown

## Consolidation calculation rules functions

### ConsolidateChildren

- Category: Consolidation calculation rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti, object:dimension, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_consolidatechildren.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ConsolidateChildren forces consolidated values to be calculated by summing immediate
children along a specified dimension. ConsolidateChildren is useful when intermediate consolidations
are calculated by rules and you want a parent consolidation to be calculated by summing the
intermediate consolidations rather than by summing the underlying leaf values.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
ConsolidateChildren(DimName1, DimName2, ...)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName1, DimName2, ... | string | Names of the dimensions along which consolidations will be performed. The function requires at least one DimName argument, and can accept as many DimName arguments as
there are dimensions in the cube for which the rule is written. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName1, DimName2, ... | Names of the dimensions along which consolidations will be performed. The function requires at least one DimName argument, and can accept as many DimName arguments as
there are dimensions in the cube for which the rule is written. |

#### Example Notes

Consider a cube named Sales composed of the dimensions ActVsBud, Region, Model, Account1, and
Month.

In this example, the Month dimension is defined as follows:

If no rule is in place for this cube, the value of the Year consolidation is calculated by
summing all the underlying leaf values, in this case Jan through Dec. The following image
illustrates this consolidation.

Now, suppose you create the following rule for this cube, which indicates that all quarterly
values should be 1:

The result is as follows:

In the following image, you can see that quarterly values are indeed calculated by the rule, but
the Year consolidation is still calculated by summing all underlying leaf values. If this is not
your desired calculation path, you can use the ConsolidateChildren function to force TM1® to calculate the Year consolidation by summing its immediate
children, specifically 1 Quarter, 2 Quarter, 3 Quarter, and 4 Quarter.

In the rule, the statement
['Year']=ConsolidateChildren('Month')
says that the
Year consolidation should be calculated by summing the immediate children of Year in the Month
dimension.

The following image shows the result of the
['Year']=ConsolidateChildren('Month')
statement:

Note that the Year consolidation is now calculated by summing its immediate children.

It's important to remember that for a given consolidation, the ConsolidateChildren function
applies only to the
immediate
children of the consolidation.

The ConsolidateChildren function can also be used to specify how consolidations are calculated in
multiple dimensions, as in the following example:

#### Examples

```ti
[{'1 Quarter', '2 Quarter', '3 Quarter', '4 Quarter'}]=1;
```

```ti
['Year']=ConsolidateChildren('Month');[{'1 Quarter', '2 Quarter', '3 Quarter', '4 Quarter'}]=1;
```

### ConsolidatedAvg

- Category: Consolidation calculation rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_consolidatedavg.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ConsolidatedAvg calculates the average value in a consolidation and returns that single
value.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
ConsolidatedAvg(flag-value, cube-name, element_1, element_2,… );
```

#### Example Notes

In a cube that is called Income Statement with three dimensions that are named Regions, Time, and
Income Statement, the Income Statement dimension contains an element that is called Gross Sales for
the overall sales number.

To calculate the average sales across all regions in the year 2010, write:

#### Examples

```ti
ConsolidatedAvg( 1,  'Income Statement', 'All Regions', '2010', 'Gross Sales' );
```

#### Arguments

The following
conditions might affect whether zeros are included in the calculation.

Name of the cube where the values reside.

If the function is running as part of a cube rule, and NOT as part of a TurboIntegrator process,
the cube-name argument can be specified as an empty string to mean the current cube. This means you
can write a rule such as
['Apr']=ConsolidatedAvg( 0, '', !actvsbud, '1 Quarter'
);

Dimension element names that define the intersection of the cube containing the consolidation for
which you want to determine the average value.

Arguments
element_1
through
element_n
are
sequence-sensitive.
element_1
must be an element from the first dimension of the
cube,
element_2
must be an element from the second dimension, and so on. These
arguments can also be the names of aliases for dimension elements or TurboIntegrator variables.

- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti

### ConsolidatedCountUnique

- Category: Consolidation calculation rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_consolidatedunique.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ConsolidatedCountUnique counts the number of unique elements for which data points
actually exist for the specified consolidation. The unique elements are counted along one dimension
of the consolidated cell.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
ConsolidatedCountUnique( flag-value, unique-along-dimension-name, cube-name,elem_1, elem_2, . . . );
```

#### Example Notes

This example uses consolidation weighting
and
ignores zero values when computing the
number of unique elements with actual values.

#### Examples

```ti
ConsolidatedCountUnique( 3, 'Regions', 'Income Statement', 'All Regions', '2010', 'Gross Sales' );
```

#### Arguments

The following conditions might affect whether
zeros are included in the calculation.

Name of the cube where the values reside.

If the function is running as part of a cube rule, and NOT as part of a TurboIntegrator process,
the cube-name argument can be specified as an empty string to mean the current cube.

Dimension element names that define the intersection of the cube which is the consolidated value
to be processed.

Arguments element_1 through element_n are sequence-sensitive. element_1 must be an element from
the first dimension of the cube, element_2 must be an element from the second dimension, and so on.
These arguments can also be the names of aliases for dimension elements or TurboIntegrator
variables.

## Cube data rules functions

### DB

- Category: Cube data rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: None
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_db.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

DB returns a value from a cube in a
Planning Analytics
database. DB returns a numeric value if used
in a numeric expression and a string value if used in a string expression.

This function is valid only in rules. Use of this function in a TurboIntegrator process will
result in an error.

- Valid in: unknown

#### Syntax

```ti
DB(cube, e1, e2, [...e256])
```

#### Example Notes

In this example, Budget is the cube name, and the function returns the value at the intersection
of California, 15" Flat Panel Monitors, Net Sales, and January.

When used to reference multi-hierarchy dimensions, you must specify the particular hierarchy. In
this example, the Category2 element exists in the ByCategory hierarchy of the ProductsCube
dimension.

#### Examples

```ti
DB('Budget', 'California', '15" Flat Panel Monitors', 'Net Sales', 'January')
```

```ti
DB('ProductsCube', 'ByCategory':'Category2',...)
```

#### Parameters

The name of the cube from which to retrieve the value.

Dimension element names that define the intersection containing the value to be retrieved.

Arguments e1 through en are sequence-sensitive. e1 must be an element from the first dimension of
the cube, e2 must be an element from the second dimension, and so on.

### ISLEAF

- Category: Cube data rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:explicit-return
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_isleaf.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ISLEAF returns 1 if a specified cell is a leaf cell (identified solely by leaf/simple
elements). If the specified cell is identified by any consolidated elements, the function returns
0.

The ISLEAF function cannot be used in TurboIntegrator processes. The presence of this function in
a process will prevent the process from compiling.

- Valid in: unknown

#### Syntax

```ti
ISLEAF
```

#### Returns

returns 1 if a specified cell is a leaf cell (identified solely by leaf/simple elements)

#### Example Notes

You can use ISLEAF in an IF statement to test if a current cell is a leaf cell. For example:

Executes the TrueStatement if the current cell is a leaf cell, otherwise it executes the
FalseStatement.

#### Examples

```ti
[]=IF((ISLEAF=1),TrueStatement, FalseStatement);
```

#### Arguments

None.

### ISUNDEFINEDCELLVALUE

- Category: Cube data rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_isundefinedcellvalue.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ISUNDEFINEDCELLVALUE compares the passed value to the default numeric cube value, which
is influenced by the presence of the UNDEFVALS declaration in that cube's rule. The function returns
1 if the passed value equals the cube's default value, otherwise the function returns 0.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Example Notes

ISUNDEFINEDCELLVALUE(TestValue)
returns 1 when TestValue is the special
undefined value and is used in the rule of a cube with UNDEFVALS declared.

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| TestValue | The numerical value to compare against the cube's default value. |
| Cube | An optional String argument that specifies the cube whose default value should be compared. When ISUNDEFINEDCELLVALUE is used in a rule, the cube is assumed to be the subject cube unless
otherwise specified. When used in a process, a cube should be specified. If the cube is omitted in a process, or is not valid when specified, 0 will be used for
comparison. |

### UNDEF

- Category: Cube data rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_undef.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

UNDEF returns the undefined value. This function can be used to prevent data from being
stored in a cube based on a logical test.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
UNDEF
```

#### Example Notes

UNDEF returns the undefined value.

#### Arguments

None.

### UNDEFINEDCELLVALUE

- Category: Cube data rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_undefinedcellvalue.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

UNDEFINEDCELLVALUE returns the default numeric cube value, which is influenced by the
presence of the UNDEFVALS declaration in that cube's rule.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Example Notes

UNDEFINEDCELLVALUE returns 0 when used in the rule of a cube without UNDEFVALS declared, or when
used in a process.

UNDEFINEDCELLVALUE returns the special undefined value when used in the rule of a cube with
UNDEFVALS declared.

UNDEFINEDCELLVALUE('ExampleCube')
returns the default value of
ExampleCube
or 0 if
ExampleCube
does not
exist.

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| Cube | An optional String argument that specifies the cube whose default value should be returned. When UNDEFINEDCELLVALUE is used in a rule, the cube is assumed to be the subject cube unless
otherwise specified. When used in a process, a cube should be specified. If the cube is omitted in a process, or is not valid when specified, 0 will be returned. |

### UNDEFVALS

- Category: Cube data rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: None
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_undefvals.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

- Valid in: unknown

#### Syntax

```ti
UNDEFVALS
```

#### Arguments

None.

#### Notes

- This
special undefined
value is not the value returned by
the UNDEF() TurboIntegrator function. The value returned by UNDEF() is an undefined value used for
such things as an attempt to divide by zero, or take the logarithm of an illegal number,
etc.

## Cube Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions

### AddCubeDependency

- Category: Cube Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:cube, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:cube, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_addcubedependency_41410.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

AddCubeDependency lets you predefine cube inter-dependencies to avoid lock contention
problems during normal system use.

In normal operations, cube dependencies are established when data which crosses cube boundaries
(such as data that is derived by a rule that references an external cube) is retrieved. To create
the dependency information, the server must lock the cubes while the dependency is established,
potentially maintaining the lock during a long view calculation. Since this is a 'write' lock, other
users are prevented from accessing the cubes. The AddCubeDependency function allows the dependency
to be established when the server starts up, preventing later lock contention as no new dependency
need be established.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
AddCubeDependency(BaseCube, DependentCube);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| BaseCube | string | The name of the cube upon which the DependentCube is dependent. |
| DependentCube | string | The name of a cube that depends on another cube (BaseCube) for data. Most commonly, this would be
a cube that uses rules to pull data from an external cube. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| BaseCube | The name of the cube upon which the DependentCube is dependent. |
| DependentCube | The name of a cube that depends on another cube (BaseCube) for data. Most commonly, this would be
a cube that uses rules to pull data from an external cube. |

#### Example Notes

Consider a cube named 'SalesCube' that includes the rule
['net']=!Units * DB('PriceCube',
... );

In this example, 'SalesCube' is the dependent cube, as it is dependent on values in the base cube
named 'PriceCube' to calculate the value of 'net'. To establish this dependency, you should run the
following function in a TurboIntegrator process:
AddCubeDependency( 'PriceCube', 'SalesCube'
);

To establish dependency at server load time, you can create a process that runs the
AddCubeDependency
function, schedule the process as a chore, and then define that
chore as one of the
StartupChores
in
Tm1s.cfg
.

### CellGetN

- Category: Cube Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:read, category:cube, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:cube, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_cellgetn.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

CellGetN retrieves a value from a numeric cube cell.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
CellGetN(Cube, e1, e2 [,...en]);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Cube | string | The name of the cube from which you want to retrieve a value. |
| e1,...e n | string | Dimension element names that define the intersection of the cube containing the value to be
retrieved. Arguments e1 through e n are sequence-sensitive. e1 must be an element from the first
dimension of the cube, e2 must be an element from the second dimension, and so on. These arguments
can also be the names of aliases for dimension elements or TurboIntegrator variables. If any of the dimensions in your cube use hierarchies, you can also use the 'HierarchyName':'ElementName' convention to specify an element within a specific
hierarchy. In this case, the sequence of arguments must still adhere to the order of dimensions in
the cube. For example, if you want to reference multiple elements from hierarchies in the second
dimension of your cube, all such arguments must appear after the argument for the first dimension in
the cube and before the argument for the third dimension in the cube. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| Cube | The name of the cube from which you want to retrieve a value. |
| e1,...e n | Dimension element names that define the intersection of the cube containing the value to be
retrieved. Arguments e1 through e n are sequence-sensitive. e1 must be an element from the first
dimension of the cube, e2 must be an element from the second dimension, and so on. These arguments
can also be the names of aliases for dimension elements or TurboIntegrator variables. If any of the dimensions in your cube use hierarchies, you can also use the 'HierarchyName':'ElementName' convention to specify an element within a specific
hierarchy. In this case, the sequence of arguments must still adhere to the order of dimensions in
the cube. For example, if you want to reference multiple elements from hierarchies in the second
dimension of your cube, all such arguments must appear after the argument for the first dimension in
the cube and before the argument for the third dimension in the cube. |

#### Example of CELLGETN and variables

When this function is used in a conditional statement (
IF
), the statement is the
portion containing the condition, not the entire conditional block. After a minor error, execution
continues with the next statement. TurboIntegrator processing has no knowledge that it was in a
conditional once the minor error is processed, so the next statement is the next line, not the line
after the
ENDIF;
.

To avoid this situation, use variables for any operation that could encounter a minor error and
then use the variables in the conditional statement.

```ti
V1 = CELLGETN('PNLCube', 'fred','argentina','Sales','Jan');
IF(V1 = 454);
    ASCIIOUTPUT('bug.txt', 'if logic not working properly');
ENDIF;
```

#### Example of CellGetN without hierarchies

This example illustrates a function that uses simple element names as arguments and does not
reference any hierarchies. It retrieves the numeric value at the intersection of the Actual,
Argentina, S Series 1.8L Sedan, Sales, and Jan elements in the Sales cube.

```ti
CellGetN('Sales', 'Actual', 'Argentina', 'S Series1.8L Sedan', 'Sales', 'Jan');
```

#### Example of CellGetN referencing multiple hierarchies

This example illustrates a function that references multiple hierarchies in the Model dimension.
It retrieves the numeric value at the intersection of the Actual, Argentina, S Series (from the
vehicles hierarchy in the model dimension), 2.8 Litre (from the enginesize hierarchy in the model
dimension), and Jan elements in the Sales cube.

```ti
CellGetN('Sales', 'Actual', 'Argentina', 
('vehicles':'S Series', 'enginesize':'2.8 Litre'), 'Sales', 'Jan');
```

#### Notes

- This example artificially breaks the line of code for easier reading.

| e1,...e n | string | Dimension element names that define the intersection of the cube to receive the value. Arguments e1 through e n are sequence-sensitive. e1 must be an element from the first
dimension of the cube, e2 must be an element from the second dimension, and so on. These arguments
can also be the names of aliases for dimension elements or TurboIntegrator variables. |

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |

| e1,...e n | Dimension element names that define the intersection of the cube to receive the value. Arguments e1 through e n are sequence-sensitive. e1 must be an element from the first
dimension of the cube, e2 must be an element from the second dimension, and so on. These arguments
can also be the names of aliases for dimension elements or TurboIntegrator variables. |

#### Example Notes

This example increments the value at the intersection of the Actual, Argentina, S Series 1.8L

```ti
CellIncrementN(1000, 'y2ksales', 'Actual', 'Argentina', 'S Series 1.8L Sedan', 'Sales', 'Jan');
```

### CellIsUpdateable

- Category: Cube Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:update, category:cube, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:cube, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_cellsupdateable.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

CellIsUpdateable determines whether a cube cell can be written to. The function returns 1
if the cell can be written to, otherwise it returns 0.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.


| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Cube | string | The name of the cube to which you want to write a value. |
| e1,...e n | string | Dimension element names that define the cell to which you want to write a value. Arguments e1 through e n are sequence-sensitive. e1 must be an element from the first
dimension of the cube, e2 must be an element from the second dimension, and so on. These arguments
can also be the names of aliases for dimension elements or TurboIntegrator variables. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| Cube | The name of the cube to which you want to write a value. |
| e1,...e n | Dimension element names that define the cell to which you want to write a value. Arguments e1 through e n are sequence-sensitive. e1 must be an element from the first
dimension of the cube, e2 must be an element from the second dimension, and so on. These arguments
can also be the names of aliases for dimension elements or TurboIntegrator variables. |

#### Example Notes

This example determines if the cell defined by the elements Actual, Argentina, S Series 1.8L
Sedan, Sales, and Jan in the y2ksales cube can be written to. If the cell can receive a value, the
function returns 1, otherwise it returns 0.

#### Examples


### CellPutN

- Category: Cube Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions

only.

| e1, e2, ..., en | string | Dimension element names that define the intersection of the cube to receive the value. Arguments e1 through en are sequence-sensitive. e1 must be an element from the first dimension of
the cube, e2 must be an element from the second dimension, and so on. These arguments can also be
the names of aliases for dimension elements or TurboIntegrator variables. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| x | A numeric value. |
| Cube | The name of the cube to which you want to send the value. |
| e1, e2, ..., en | Dimension element names that define the intersection of the cube to receive the value. Arguments e1 through en are sequence-sensitive. e1 must be an element from the first dimension of
the cube, e2 must be an element from the second dimension, and so on. These arguments can also be
the names of aliases for dimension elements or TurboIntegrator variables. |

#### Example Notes

This example sends the value 12345 to the intersection of the Actual, Argentina, S Series 1.8L
Sedan, Sales, and Jan elements in the y2ksales cube.

#### Examples

```ti
CellPutN(12345, 'y2ksales', 'Actual', 'Argentina', 'S Series 1.8L Sedan', 'Sales', 'Jan');
```

#### Notes

- If you supply invalid arguments to the
CellPutN()
function in a
TurboIntegrator process when the cube does not exist, an error is sent to the
tm1server.log
.

### CellPutProportionalSpread

- Category: Cube Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:update, category:cube, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:cube, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_cellputproportionalspread.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

CellPutProportionalSpread distributes a specified value to the leaves of a consolidation
proportional to existing cell values. CellPutProportionalSpread replaces existing cell values; it
cannot be used to add to or subtract from existing cell values.

The function is analogous to the Proportional Spread data spreading method. If you must add to or
subtract from existing cell values, use the Proportional Spread method, which can be executed
through the user interface or through data spreading syntax.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
CellPutProportionalSpread( value, cube, e1, e2, e3...,en );
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| value | unknown | The value you want to distribute. |
| cube | string | The name of the cube into which you want to distribute the value. |
| e1...e n | string | The names of the elements that identify the consolidation whose leaves will accept the
distributed value. Arguments e1 through e n are sequence-sensitive. e1 must be an element from the first
dimension of the cube, e2 must be an element from the second dimension, and so on. These arguments
can also be the names of aliases for dimension elements or TurboIntegrator variables. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| value | The value you want to distribute. |
| cube | The name of the cube into which you want to distribute the value. |
| e1...e n | The names of the elements that identify the consolidation whose leaves will accept the
distributed value. Arguments e1 through e n are sequence-sensitive. e1 must be an element from the first
dimension of the cube, e2 must be an element from the second dimension, and so on. These arguments
can also be the names of aliases for dimension elements or TurboIntegrator variables. |

#### Example Notes

This example distributes the value 7000 to the children of the consolidation in the SalesCube
identified by the elements Actual, North America, S Series 1.8L Sedan, Sales, and Jan.

#### Examples

```ti
CellPutProportionalSpread(7000,'SalesCube', 'Actual','North America', 
'S Series 1.8L Sedan', 'Sales', 'Jan')
```

#### Notes

- When using CellPutProportionalSpread to distribute a value to the leaves of a consolidation,
only those leaves already containing non-zero values are changed. This is because zero values cannot
be incremented or decremented proportionally; any proportion of zero is still zero.

### CubeCreate

- Category: Cube Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-10-15
- Tags: action:create, category:cube, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:cube, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_cubecreate.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

CubeCreate creates a cube from specified dimensions. The order of dimensions specified in
the function will be the order of dimensions in the cube definition. After execution, CubeCreate
automatically saves the resulting .cub file to disk.

This function is valid in TM1®
TurboIntegrator
processes only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
CubeCreate(Cube, d1, d2 [,...dn]);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Cube | string | The name you want to assign to the cube. |
| d1,...d n | string | The names of dimensions that comprise the cube. You must specify at least two, but no more than
256, dimensions. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| Cube | The name you want to assign to the cube. |
| d1,...d n | The names of dimensions that comprise the cube. You must specify at least two, but no more than
256, dimensions. |

#### Example Notes

This example creates a cube named y2ksales using the dimensions Actvsbud, Region, Model,
Account1, and Month.

#### Examples

```ti
CubeCreate('y2ksales', 'Actvsbud', 'Region', 'Model','Account1', 'Month');
```

#### Notes

- When you create a cube using the REST API, transaction logging is enabled
on the new cube. The
Planning Analytics Workspace
modeling
workbench uses the REST API for all interactions with
TM1
. However, if you create a cube with the CubeCreate
TurboIntegrator
function, transaction logging
is not enabled. To enable transaction logging, use the CubeSetLogChanges
TurboIntegrator
function.

### CubeExists

### CubeTimeLastUpdated

- Category: Cube Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:update, category:cube, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:cube, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ti_func_cubetimelastupdated.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

CubeTimeLastUpdated returns a serial value that indicates the date and time at which a
specified cube was last updated.

The serial value that is returned by this function uses a starting time of Jan 1 1900 12:00:00
A.M., which is equivalent to the value 1.0. Dates are represented by integers, while times are
represented as decimal numbers between .0 and .999999. This is consistent with the way date and time
serial values are stored and reported in Microsoft
Excel.

This function is valid in TM1 TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
CubeTimeLastUpdated(cube);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| cube | string | The name of the cube. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| cube | The name of the cube. |

#### Example Notes

This example returns a value corresponding to the time when the Sales cube was last updated.

#### Examples

```ti
CubeTimeLastUpdated('Sales');
```

#### Notes

- By default, TM1® date and time serial values use a
starting time of Jan 1 1960 12:00:00 A.M. To resolve the inconsistency between Excel and TM1 date
and time serial values, you can set
UseExcelSerialDate=T
in your Tm1s.cfg file
to instruct the TM1 server to use date and time serial values that conform to Excel
standards.

### CubeUnload

- Category: Cube Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:cube, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:cube, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_cubeunload.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

CubeUnload unloads a specified cube, along with all associated cube views, from memory.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
CubeUnload(CubeName);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| CubeName | string | The cube you want to unload from memory. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| CubeName | The cube you want to unload from memory. |

#### Example Notes

This example unloads the ManufacturingBudget cube, and any associated views, from server
memory.

#### Examples

```ti
CubeUnload('ManufacturingBudget');
```

### TurboIntegrator Functions

- Category: Cube Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:cube
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/c_tm1turbointegratorfunctions_n70006.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

TurboIntegrator lets you manipulate
Planning Analytics
data and metadata when you define a
process.

This is accomplished through the use of functions in the Prolog, Metadata, Data, and Epilog
sub-tabs within the Advanced tab of the TurboIntegrator window. These sub-tabs include generated
statements based on settings and options you select when defining a TurboIntegrator process. Any
functions you create must appear after the generated statements. For details on creating processes
with TurboIntegrator, see the
TurboIntegrator
documentation.

- Valid in: unknown

## Date and time rules functions

### DATE

- Category: Date and time rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti, value:number, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_date.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

DATE returns the date string in
yy-mm-dd
or
yyyy-mm-dd
format for a given serial number.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
DATE(SerialNumber, ReturnFourDigitYear)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| SerialNumber | number | A date expressed in serial format. |
| ReturnFourDigitYear | string | An optional Boolean argument that determines whether the DATE function returns a string using
two- or four-digit notation for the year. If ReturnFourDigitYear is true, the function returns date falling within the range of Jan. 1,
1960 and Dec. 31, 9999, using four-digit notation for the year. Serial date 0 corresponds to Jan. 1,
1960 and serial date 2936549 corresponds to Dec. 31, 9999. If ReturnFourDigitYear is false, or if this optional argument is omitted from the DATE function,
the function returns a date falling within the range Jan. 1, 1960 and Dec. 31, 2059, using two-digit
notation for the year. Serial date 0 corresponds to Jan 1, 1960 and serial date 36524 corresponds to
Dec. 31, 2059. If ReturnFourDigitYear is false or is omitted and you specify a serial date greater than 36524,
the serial date used by the function is determined by the formula n - 36525. For example, if you
specify a serial date of 36530, then 36530 - 36525 = 5. In this case, DATE uses 5 as the serial date
and returns the date Jan. 6, 1960. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| SerialNumber | A date expressed in serial format. |
| ReturnFourDigitYear | An optional Boolean argument that determines whether the DATE function returns a string using
two- or four-digit notation for the year. If ReturnFourDigitYear is true, the function returns date falling within the range of Jan. 1,
1960 and Dec. 31, 9999, using four-digit notation for the year. Serial date 0 corresponds to Jan. 1,
1960 and serial date 2936549 corresponds to Dec. 31, 9999. If ReturnFourDigitYear is false, or if this optional argument is omitted from the DATE function,
the function returns a date falling within the range Jan. 1, 1960 and Dec. 31, 2059, using two-digit
notation for the year. Serial date 0 corresponds to Jan 1, 1960 and serial date 36524 corresponds to
Dec. 31, 2059. If ReturnFourDigitYear is false or is omitted and you specify a serial date greater than 36524,
the serial date used by the function is determined by the formula n - 36525. For example, if you
specify a serial date of 36530, then 36530 - 36525 = 5. In this case, DATE uses 5 as the serial date
and returns the date Jan. 6, 1960. |

#### Example Notes

DATE(13947) returns
98-03-09
.

DATE(13947, 1) returns
1998-03-09
.

### DATES

- Category: Date and time rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_dates.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

DATES returns a date string, in the form 'yy-mm-dd' or 'yyyy-mm-dd', corresponding to a
given year, month, and day.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
DATES(year, month, day)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| year | unknown | A year, expressed in either yy or yyyy format. |
| month | unknown | A month, expressed in mm format. |
| day | unknown | A day, expressed in dd format. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| year | A year, expressed in either yy or yyyy format. |
| month | A month, expressed in mm format. |
| day | A day, expressed in dd format. |

#### Example Notes

DATES(98, 2, 10) returns '98-02-10'.

DATES(1998, 2, 10) returns '1998-02-10'.

### DAY

- Category: Date and time rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_day.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

DAY returns a numeric value for the day in a given date string.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
DAY(DateString)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DateString | string | A date string in either YY-MM-DD or YYYY-MM-DD format. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DateString | A date string in either YY-MM-DD or YYYY-MM-DD format. |

#### Example Notes

DAY('02-05-25') returns 25.

### DAYNO

- Category: Date and time rules functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_dayno.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

DAYNO returns the serial date number corresponding to a given date string.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
DAYNO('DateString')
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DateString | string | A date string in either YY-MM-DD or YYYY-MM-DD format. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DateString | A date string in either YY-MM-DD or YYYY-MM-DD format. |

#### Example Notes

DAYNO('98-03-09') returns 13947.

#### Notes

- DAYNO can return serial dates for date strings starting at January 1, 1960 (dates
string 1960-01-01 or 60-01-01). For dates after December 31, 2059, you use a four digit year in the
date string. For example, the date string for January 5, 2061 would be 2061-01-05.
