### ElementType

- Category: Element Information Rules Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_elementtype.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ElementType returns information about the element type of a specified
element.

ElementType returns N if the element is a numeric element, S if the element is a string element,
and C if the element is a consolidated element.

In the case of an element attribute dimension, ElementType returns AN if the attribute is a
numeric attribute, AS if the attribute is a string attribute, and AA if the attribute is an alias
attribute. For more information, see
Element Attributes
.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
ElementType(dimension, hierarchy, element)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| dimension | string | A valid dimension name. |
| hierarchy | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| element | string | The name of an element within the dimension. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| dimension | A valid dimension name. |
| hierarchy | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| element | The name of an element within the dimension. |

#### Example Notes

The element Europe is a consolidated element of the Region dimension, so the example returns
C.

#### Examples

```ti
ElementType('Region', 'Countries', 'Europe')
```

### ElementWeight

- Category: Element Information Rules Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string

### ELISCOMP

- Category: Element Information Rules Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:explicit-return, feature:rules-and-ti, object:dimension, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_eliscomp.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ELISCOMP determines whether element1 is a child of element2 in the specified dimension.
The function returns 1 if element1 is a child of element2, otherwise the function returns 0.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
ELISCOMP(dimension, element1, element2)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| dimension | string | A valid dimension name. |
| element1 | string | The name of an element within the dimension. |
| element2 | string | The name of an element within the dimension. |

#### Returns

returns 1 if element1 is a child of element2, otherwise the function returns 0

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| dimension | A valid dimension name. |
| element1 | The name of an element within the dimension. |
| element2 | The name of an element within the dimension. |

#### Example Notes

In the dimension Region, the element Central Europe is a consolidation of two elements, Germany
and France. The following example returns 1.

However, because the function returns 1 only for immediate children, the following example
returns 0:

#### Examples

```ti
ELISCOMP('Region','Germany','Central Europe')
```

```ti
ELISCOMP('Region','Germany','Europe')
```

#### Notes

- this function returns 1 only for immediate children. In this example, Germany is a
child of Central Europe. Further, Central Europe is a child of Europe.

### ELISPAR

- Category: Element Information Rules Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:explicit-return, feature:rules-and-ti, object:dimension, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_elispar.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ELISPAR determines whether element1 is a parent of element2 in the specified dimension.
The function returns 1 if element1 is a parent of element2, otherwise the function returns 0.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
ELISPAR(dimension, element1, element2)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| dimension | string | A valid dimension name. |
| element1 | string | The name of an element within the dimension. |
| element2 | string | The name of an element within the dimension. |

#### Returns

returns 1 if element1 is a parent of element2, otherwise the function returns 0

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| dimension | A valid dimension name. |
| element1 | The name of an element within the dimension. |
| element2 | The name of an element within the dimension. |

#### Example Notes

In the dimension Region, the consolidated element Central Europe is the parent of both Germany
and France. Accordingly, the following example returns 1.

However, because Europe is not an immediate parent of Germany, the following example returns
0:

#### Examples

```ti
ELISPAR('Region','Central Europe','Germany')
```

```ti
ELISPAR('Region','Europe','Germany')
```

#### Notes

- this function returns 1 only for immediate parents. In this example, Europe is a
parent of Central Europe. Further, Central Europe is a parent of Germany.

### ELLEV

- Category: Element Information Rules Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti, object:dimension, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_ellev.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ELLEV returns the level of an element within a dimension.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
ELLEV(dimension, element)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| dimension | string | A valid dimension name. |
| element | string | The name of an element within the dimension. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| dimension | A valid dimension name. |
| element | The name of an element within the dimension. |

#### Example Notes

In the Region dimension, individual nations (Level 0) add up to regions (Level 1). The regions
then add up to super-regions (Level 2), which in turn add up to the world (Level 3). The example
returns 2, as Europe is a Level 2 element.

#### Examples

```ti
ELLEV('Region','Europe')
```

### ELPAR

- Category: Element Information Rules Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti, object:dimension, value:number, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_elpar.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ELPAR returns the parent of an element in a specified dimension.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
ELPAR(dimension, element, index)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| dimension | string | A valid dimension name. |
| element | string | The name of an element within the dimension. |
| index | number | A positive value less than or equal to the total number of consolidated elements (parents) that
use the element argument as a child. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| dimension | A valid dimension name. |
| element | The name of an element within the dimension. |
| index | A positive value less than or equal to the total number of consolidated elements (parents) that
use the element argument as a child. |

#### Example Notes

In the dimension Model, the element Wagon 4WD is a child of both Total Wagons and Total 4WD.
Therefore, both Total Wagons and Total 4WD are parents of Wagon 4WD. In the structure of the Model
dimension, Total Wagons is defined first, Total 4WD is defined second.

The example returns Total 4WD, as this is the second instance of a parent to Wagon 4WD within the
Model dimension.

#### Examples

```ti
ELPAR('Model','Wagon 4WD',2)
```

### ELWEIGHT

### LevelCount

- Category: Element Information Rules Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_levelcount.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

LevelCount returns the number levels in a dimension.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
LevelCount(dimension, hierarchy)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| dimension | string | A valid dimension name. Some installations may need to qualify the dimension name with the database name, as in database_name:dimension . |
| hierarchy | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| dimension | A valid dimension name. Some installations may need to qualify the dimension name with the database name, as in database_name:dimension . |
| hierarchy | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |

#### Example Notes

In the Region dimension, the various nations (Level 0) add up to regions (Level 1). The regions
then add up to super-regions (Level 2), which in turn add up to the world (Level 3).

There are four levels in the Region dimension, so the example returns the value 4.

#### Examples

```ti
LevelCount('Region', 'Countries')
```

## Financial Rules Functions

### FV

- Category: Financial Rules Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti, value:number
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_fv.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

FV returns the value of an annuity at the time of the last payment. An annuity is a
series of payments made at equal intervals of time. Payments are assumed to be made at the end of
each period.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
FV(payment, interest, periods)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| payment | unknown | The amount of the payment made per period. |
| interest | unknown | The interest rate paid per period. |
| periods | number | The number of periods in the annuity. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| payment | The amount of the payment made per period. |
| interest | The interest rate paid per period. |
| periods | The number of periods in the annuity. |

#### Example Notes

This example returns the value of an annuity at the end of 5 years, with payments of $1,000 per
year at 14% interest.

#### Examples

```ti
FV(1000, .14, 5)
```

### PAYMT

- Category: Financial Rules Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti, value:number
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_paymt.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

PAYMT returns the payment amount of an annuity based on a given initial value or
principal, an interest rate, and a number of periods. An annuity is a series of payments made at
equal intervals of time.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
PAYMT(principal, interest, periods)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| principal | unknown | The present value, or the total amount that a series of future payments is worth now. |
| interest | unknown | The interest rate paid per period. |
| periods | number | The number of periods in the annuity. Payments are assumed to be made at the end of each
period. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| principal | The present value, or the total amount that a series of future payments is worth now. |
| interest | The interest rate paid per period. |
| periods | The number of periods in the annuity. Payments are assumed to be made at the end of each
period. |

#### Example Notes

This example returns the payment on a 5-year annuity that is paid yearly, with a principal of
$100,000 at 14% interest.

#### Examples

```ti
PAYMT(100000, .14, 5)
```

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |

| interest | The interest rate paid per period. |

## Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions

### HierarchyContainsAllLeaves

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchycontainsallleaves.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyContainsAllLeaves returns true only if the specified hierarchy contains the full
set of leaf elements that are present in the dimension. That is, it contains all the leaf elements
that can be seen in the special Leaves hierarchy. If the specified hierarchy is missing one or more
leaf elements, this function returns false.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyContainsAllLeaves(DimName, HierName);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The name of the dimension that contains the all leaves hierarchy. |
| HierName | string | The name of the hierarchy you are determining as an all leaves hierarchy. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The name of the dimension that contains the all leaves hierarchy. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy you are determining as an all leaves hierarchy. |

#### Example Notes

This example determines if the Leaves hierarchy, in the Region dimension, contains all leaf
members.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchyContainsAllLeaves('Region', 'Leaves');
```

### HierarchyCreate

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:create, category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string

#### Description

HierarchyCreate creates a new hierarchy in an existing dimension. The hierarchy cannot
have the same name as the dimension.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyCreate(DimName, HierName);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The name of the existing dimension that will contain the hierarchy. |
| HierName | string | The name you want to assign to the hierarchy. You cannot use the name of the dimension. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The name of the existing dimension that will contain the hierarchy. |
| HierName | The name you want to assign to the hierarchy. You cannot use the name of the dimension. |

#### Example Notes

This example creates the empty Trucks hierarchy in the Vehicles dimension.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchyCreate('Vehicles', 'Trucks');
```

### HierarchyDeleteAllElements

### HierarchyDeleteElements

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:delete, category:hierarchy, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, object:subset, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchydeleteelements.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyDeleteElements deletes elements from a hierarchy using a subset of
elements.

This function is valid only in TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: unknown

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyDeleteElements (DimensionName, HierarchyName, Subset)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimensionName | string | The name of the dimension from which you want to delete the subset of elements. |
| HierarchyName | string | The name of the hierarchy from which you want to delete the subset of elements. If the indicated hierarchy is the Leaves hierarchy, then the subset should list those leaves that
should be deleted, and they are removed completely from the dimension. |
| Subset | string | The name of the subset that contains the elements you want to delete. The function deletes all
elements in the subset from the specified hierarchy, whether leaf or consolidated. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimensionName | The name of the dimension from which you want to delete the subset of elements. |
| HierarchyName | The name of the hierarchy from which you want to delete the subset of elements. If the indicated hierarchy is the Leaves hierarchy, then the subset should list those leaves that
should be deleted, and they are removed completely from the dimension. |
| Subset | The name of the subset that contains the elements you want to delete. The function deletes all
elements in the subset from the specified hierarchy, whether leaf or consolidated. |

### HierarchyElementComponentAdd

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchyelementcomponentadd.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyElementComponentAdd adds a component (child) to a consolidated element. You
can't use this function in the Epilog procedure of a TurboIntegrator process.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyElementComponentAdd(DimName, HierName, ConsolidatedElName, ElName, ElWeight);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The parent dimension of the consolidated element to which you want to add a child. |
| HierName | string | The hierarchy of the specified dimension. |
| ConsolidatedElName | string | The element to which you want to add a child. |
| ElName | string | The name of the child element. |
| ElWeight | unknown | The weight of the child element. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The parent dimension of the consolidated element to which you want to add a child. |
| HierName | The hierarchy of the specified dimension. |
| ConsolidatedElName | The element to which you want to add a child. |
| ElName | The name of the child element. |
| ElWeight | The weight of the child element. |

#### Example Notes

This example adds the child Expenses to the Net Sales
consolidation in the Europe hierarchy of the Measures dimension. The child has a weight of -1 in the
consolidation.

### HierarchyElementComponentAddDirect

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchyelementcomponentadddirect.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyElementComponentAddDirect adds a component (child) to a consolidated element by
directly editing a dimension.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

The default method of editing a dimension in Cognos®
TM1 is to use a whole-copy editing pattern. In that pattern,
an editing copy of the dimension is created, edits are applied to the editing copy, then finally the
actual dimension is rewritten using the editing copy as a template. TurboIntegrator supports
whole-copy editing automatically whenever dimension editing TurboIntegrator functions (like
HierarchyElementComponentAdd) are used in the Metadata procedure of the process. TurboIntegrator
automatically creates the editing copy and applies editing operations to it, then rewrites the
actual dimension at the end of the Metadata procedure.

Direct edits are different in that no editing copy is involved. Instead, the operations are
performed directly on the actual dimension. There are two different, specialized use cases for which
this type of direct editing is intended:

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyElementComponentAddDirect(DimName, HierName, ConsolidatedElName, ElName, ElWeight);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The parent dimension of the consolidated element to which you want to add a child. |
| HierName | string | The hierarchy of the specified dimension. |
| ConsolidatedElName | string | The consolidated element to which you want to add a child. |
| ElName | string | The name of the child element. |
| ElWeight | unknown | The weight of the child element. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The parent dimension of the consolidated element to which you want to add a child. |
| HierName | The hierarchy of the specified dimension. |
| ConsolidatedElName | The consolidated element to which you want to add a child. |
| ElName | The name of the child element. |
| ElWeight | The weight of the child element. |

#### Example Notes

This example adds the child Expenses to the Net Sales
consolidation in the Europe hierarchy of the Measures dimension. The child has a weight of -1 in the
consolidation.

### HierarchyElementComponentDelete

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:delete, category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchyelementcomponentdelete.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyElementComponentDelete deletes a component (child) from a consolidated
element.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyElementComponentDelete(DimName, HierName, ConsolidatedElName, ElName);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The parent dimension of the consolidated element from which you want to delete a child. |
| HierName | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| ConsolidatedElName | string | The consolidated element from which you want to delete a child. |
| ElName | string | The name of the child element you want to delete. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The parent dimension of the consolidated element from which you want to delete a child. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| ConsolidatedElName | The consolidated element from which you want to delete a child. |
| ElName | The name of the child element you want to delete. |

#### Example Notes

the Region dimension.


### HierarchyElementComponentDeleteDirect

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:delete, category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchyelementcomponentdeletedirect.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyElementComponentDeleteDirect deletes a component (child) from a consolidated
element by directly editing the dimension.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

The default method of editing a dimension in TM1 is to use
a whole-copy editing pattern. In that pattern, an editing copy of the dimension is created, edits
are applied to the editing copy, then finally the actual dimension is rewritten using the editing
copy as a template. TurboIntegrator supports whole-copy editing automatically whenever dimension
editing TurboIntegrator functions (like HierarchyElementComponentDelete) are used in the Metadata
procedure of the process. TurboIntegrator automatically creates the editing copy and applies editing
operations to it, then rewrites the actual dimension at the end of the Metadata procedure.

Direct edits are different in that no editing copy is involved. Instead, the operations are
performed directly on the actual dimension. There are two different, specialized use cases for which
this type of direct editing is intended:

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyElementComponentDeleteDirect(DimName, HierName, ConsolidatedElName, ElName);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The parent dimension of the consolidated element from which you want to delete a child. |
| HierName | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| ConsolidatedElName | string | The consolidated element from which you want to delete a child. |
| ElName | string | The name of the child element you want to delete. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The parent dimension of the consolidated element from which you want to delete a child. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| ConsolidatedElName | The consolidated element from which you want to delete a child. |
| ElName | The name of the child element you want to delete. |

#### Example Notes

This example deletes the Belgium child from the Benelux consolidation in the Western hierarchy of
the Region dimension.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchyElementComponentDeleteDirect('Region', 'Western', 'Benelux', 'Belgium');
```

### HierarchyElementDelete

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19

#### Description

HierarchyElementDelete deletes an element from a hierarchy.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyElementDelete(DimName, HierName, ElName);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The dimension that contains the element you want to delete. |
| HierName | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| ElName | string | The element you want to delete from the hierarchy. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The dimension that contains the element you want to delete. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| ElName | The element you want to delete from the hierarchy. |

#### Example Notes

This example deletes the element Belgium from the Western hierarchy in the Region dimension.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchyElementDelete('Region', 'Western', 'Belgium');
```

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions

#### Description

HierarchyElementDeleteDirect deletes an element from a dimension by directly editing the
dimension.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

The default means of editing a dimension in TM1 is to use a
whole-copy editing pattern. In that pattern, an editing copy of the dimension is created, edits are
applied to the editing copy, then finally the actual dimension is rewritten using the editing copy
as a template. TurboIntegrator supports whole-copy editing automatically whenever dimension editing
TurboIntegrator functions (like DimensionElementDelete) are used in the Metadata procedure of the
process. TurboIntegrator automatically creates the editing copy and applies editing operations to
it, then rewrites the actual dimension at the end of the Metadata procedure.

Direct edits are different in that no editing copy is involved. Instead, the operations are
performed directly on the actual dimension. There are two different, specialized use cases for which
this type of direct editing is intended:

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyElementDeleteDirect(DimName, HierName, ElName);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |

| HierName | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| ElName | string | The element you want to delete. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The dimension that contains the element you want to delete. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| ElName | The element you want to delete. |

#### Example Notes

This example deletes the element Belgium from the Western hierarchy in the Region dimension.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchyElementDeleteDirect('Region', 'Western', 'Belgium');
```

### HierarchyElementExists

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:read, category:hierarchy, feature:explicit-return, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ti_func_hierarchyelementexists.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyElementExists determines whether a specific elements exists in a hierarchy on
the server from which a TurboIntegrator process is executed. The function returns 1 if the elements
exists in the hierarchy on the server, otherwise it returns 0.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyElementExists(DimName, HierName, ElemName);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The name of the dimension that contains the element whose existence you want to confirm. |
| HierName | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| ElName | string | The element you want to find in the hierarchy. |

#### Returns

returns 1 if the elements exists in the hierarchy on the server, otherwise it returns 0

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The name of the dimension that contains the element whose existence you want to confirm. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| ElName | The element you want to find in the hierarchy. |

#### Example Notes

This example determines whether element Belgium from the Western hierarchy in the Region
dimension exists on the server.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchyElementExists('Region', 'Western', 'Belgium');
```

### HierarchyElementInsert

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:create, category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:number, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchyelementinsert.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyElementInsert adds an element to a dimension. You can use this function to add
numeric, string, or consolidated elements. You can't use this function in the Data or Epilog
procedures of a TurboIntegrator process.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyElementInsert(DimName, HierName, InsertionPoint, ElName, ElType);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The dimension to which you want to add a new element. |
| HierName | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| InsertionPoint | string | An existing dimension element. The element being added to the dimension will be inserted
immediately before this existing element. If this parameter is empty, the new element is added to
the end of the dimension. |
| ElName | string | The name you want to assign to the new element. |
| ElType | number | The element type. There are three possible ElType values: N - Signifies a numeric element. S - Signifies a string element. C - Signifies a consolidated element. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The dimension to which you want to add a new element. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| InsertionPoint | An existing dimension element. The element being added to the dimension will be inserted
immediately before this existing element. If this parameter is empty, the new element is added to
the end of the dimension. |
| ElName | The name you want to assign to the new element. |
| ElType | The element type. There are three possible ElType values: N - Signifies a numeric element. S - Signifies a string element. C - Signifies a consolidated element. |

#### Example Notes

This example adds the numeric element Netherlands to the Western hierarchy in the Region
dimension. Netherland displays immediately before Belgium in the dimension definition.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchyElementInsert('Region', 'Western', 'Belgium', 'Netherlands','N');
```

### HierarchyElementInsertDirect

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:create, category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:number, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchyelementinsertdirect.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyElementInsertDirect adds an element to a dimension by directly editing the
dimension. You can use this function to add numeric, string, or consolidated elements.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

The default means of editing a dimension in TM1 is to use a
whole-copy editing pattern. In that pattern, an editing copy of the dimension is created, edits are
applied to the editing copy, then finally the actual dimension is rewritten using the editing copy
as a template. TurboIntegrator supports whole-copy editing automatically whenever dimension editing
TurboIntegrator functions (like HierarchyElementInsert) are used in the metadata tab of the process.
TurboIntegrator automatically creates the editing copy and applies editing operations to it, then
rewrites the actual dimension at the end of the Metadata procedure.

Direct edits are different in that no editing copy is involved. Instead, the operations are
performed directly on the actual dimension. There are two different, specialized use cases for which
this type of direct editing is intended:

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyElementInsertDirect(DimName, HierName, InsertionPoint, ElName, ElType);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The dimension to which you want to add a new element. |
| HierName | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| InsertionPoint | string | An existing dimension element. The element being added to the dimension will be inserted
immediately before this existing element. If this parameter is empty, the new element is added to
the end of the dimension. Note that this function is optimized for the case where the InsertionPoint is passed as an empty
string. |
| ElName | string | The name you want to assign to the new element. |
| ElType | number | The element type. There are three possible ElType values: N - Signifies a numeric element. S - Signifies a string element. C - Signifies a consolidated element. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The dimension to which you want to add a new element. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| InsertionPoint | An existing dimension element. The element being added to the dimension will be inserted
immediately before this existing element. If this parameter is empty, the new element is added to
the end of the dimension. Note that this function is optimized for the case where the InsertionPoint is passed as an empty
string. |
| ElName | The name you want to assign to the new element. |
| ElType | The element type. There are three possible ElType values: N - Signifies a numeric element. S - Signifies a string element. C - Signifies a consolidated element. |

#### Example Notes

This example adds the numeric element Netherlands to the Western hierarchy in the Region
dimension. Netherlands displays immediately before Belgium in the dimension definition.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchyElementInsertDirect('Region', 'Western', 'Belgium', 'Netherlands','N');
```

### HierarchyElementPrincipalName

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchyelementprincipalname.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyElementPrincipalName returns the principal name of an element or element
alias.

TurboIntegrator must use principal element names when updating dimensions; element aliases cannot
be used. This function is therefore useful for determining principal element names while attempting
to update a dimension when only element aliases are available to the TurboIntegrator process.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyElementPrincipalName( DimName, HierName, ElName )
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The name of the dimension from which you want to retrieve a principal element name. |
| HierName | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| ElName | string | An element name. ElName can be either an element alias or a principal element name. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The name of the dimension from which you want to retrieve a principal element name. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| ElName | An element name. ElName can be either an element alias or a principal element name. |

#### Example Notes

If ElName is not in the currently saved version of DimName, the function returns ElName.

If ElName is in DimName, whether as an element alias or a principal element name, it returns the
principal name of the element.

### HierarchyExists

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions

### HierarchyHasOrphanedLeaves

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-09-03
- Tags: category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchyhasorphanedleaves.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyHasOrphanedLeaves returns an integer that represents the number of members in the
specified hierarchy that are not components of a parent member in that hierarchy (that is, orphaned
leaves). If there are no members, the function returns 0.

This function is valid in TurboIntegrator processes only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyHasOrphanedLeaves(DimName, HierName);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The name of the dimension that contains the hierarchy being reviewed. |
| HierName | string | The name of the hierarchy you are reviewing for orphaned leaf members. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The name of the dimension that contains the hierarchy being reviewed. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy you are reviewing for orphaned leaf members. |

#### Example Notes

This example determines if the Europe hierarchy, in the Region dimension, contains any orphaned
leaves.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchyHasOrphanedLeaves('Region', 'Europe');
```

### HierarchySortOrder

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchysortorder.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchySortOrder sets a sort type and sense for dimension elements and for components
of consolidated elements within a dimension. The sort order defined by DimensionSortOrder determines
how the subset displays in the Subset Editor.

DimensionSortOrder sets properties for a dimension; the dimension is not actually sorted until it
is saved on the server.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchySortOrder(DimName, HierName, CompSortType, CompSortSense,ElSortType , ElSortSense);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The name of the dimension for which you want to set a sort order. |
| HierName | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| CompSortType | string | Defines how components of consolidated elements appear in the dimension. There are two
CompSortType values: ByInput - Retains the order in which components were originally inserted into consolidations. ByName - Sorts components of consolidations by name. |
| CompSortSense | string | Defines the sort sense for components of consolidations. This is a required argument, but it
applies only when the CompSortType is ByName. There are two possible CompSortSense values: Ascending - Sorts components of consolidations in ascending alphabetical order. Descending - Sorts components of consolidations in descending alphabetical order. |
| ElSortType | string | Defines a sort order for dimension elements. There are four possible ElSortType values: ByInput - Retains the order in which elements were originally inserted into the dimension. ByName - Sorts dimension elements by name. ByLevel - Sorts dimension elements by level. ByHierarchy - Sorts dimension elements by hierarchy. |
| ElSortSense | string | Defines the sort sense for dimension elements. This is a required argument, but it applies only
when the ElSortType is ByName or ByLevel. There are two possible ElSortSense values: Ascending - Sorts dimension elements in ascending order, either alphabetically or by level. Descending - Sorts dimension elements in descending order, either alphabetically or by level. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The name of the dimension for which you want to set a sort order. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| CompSortType | Defines how components of consolidated elements appear in the dimension. There are two
CompSortType values: ByInput - Retains the order in which components were originally inserted into consolidations. ByName - Sorts components of consolidations by name. |
| CompSortSense | Defines the sort sense for components of consolidations. This is a required argument, but it
applies only when the CompSortType is ByName. There are two possible CompSortSense values: Ascending - Sorts components of consolidations in ascending alphabetical order. Descending - Sorts components of consolidations in descending alphabetical order. |
| ElSortType | Defines a sort order for dimension elements. There are four possible ElSortType values: ByInput - Retains the order in which elements were originally inserted into the dimension. ByName - Sorts dimension elements by name. ByLevel - Sorts dimension elements by level. ByHierarchy - Sorts dimension elements by hierarchy. |
| ElSortSense | Defines the sort sense for dimension elements. This is a required argument, but it applies only
when the ElSortType is ByName or ByLevel. There are two possible ElSortSense values: Ascending - Sorts dimension elements in ascending order, either alphabetically or by level. Descending - Sorts dimension elements in descending order, either alphabetically or by level. |

#### Example Notes

This example sets a sort order for the Europe hierarchy in the Region dimension. All dimension
elements are sorted by level in ascending order, and any components of consolidations are sorted in
descending alphabetical order.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchySortOrder ('Region', 'Europe', 'ByName', 'Descending','ByLevel', 'Ascending');
```

### HierarchyTimeLastUpdated

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:update, category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchytimelastupdated.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyTimeLastUpdated indicates when a specified dimension hierarchy was last updated.
The function returns a real number that represents the current day (including the hour, minute,
second, and millisecond) since the beginning of the year 1900.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyTimeLastUpdated(dimension, hierarchy);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| dimension | string | The name of the dimension. |
| hierarchy | string | The name of the hierarchy. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| dimension | The name of the dimension. |
| hierarchy | The name of the hierarchy. |

#### Example Notes

This example returns information on when the Europe hierarchy of the Region dimension was last
updated. If a value of 42548.<hours>.<minutes>.<milliseconds> is returned, you can divide
42548 by 365 to obtain (approximately) 116. When added to the started of 1900, the result is a
current year of 2016.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchyTimeLastUpdated('Region', 'Europe');
```

### HierarchyTopElementInsert

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:create, category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchytopelementinsert.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyTopElementInsert creates a root element in a dimension. If the dimension already
has a single root, then this element will not be created.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyTopElementInsert(DimName, HierName, InsertionPoint, ElName);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The dimension for which you want to create a root element. |
| HierName | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| InsertionPoint | string | An existing dimension element. The root element being added to the dimension will be inserted
immediately before this existing element. |
| ElName | string | The name you want to assign to the new root element. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The dimension for which you want to create a root element. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| InsertionPoint | An existing dimension element. The root element being added to the dimension will be inserted
immediately before this existing element. |
| ElName | The name you want to assign to the new root element. |

#### Example Notes

This example adds the root element World to the Western hierarchy of the Region dimension. World
is inserted displays immediately before Netherlands in the dimension definition.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchyTopElementInsert('Region', 'Western', 'Netherlands', 'World');
```

### HierarchyTopElementInsertDirect

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:create, category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string

| InsertionPoint | string | An existing dimension element. The root element being added to the dimension will be inserted
immediately before this existing element. |
| ElName | string | The name you want to assign to the new root element. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The dimension for which you want to create a root element. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |
| InsertionPoint | An existing dimension element. The root element being added to the dimension will be inserted
immediately before this existing element. |
| ElName | The name you want to assign to the new root element. |

#### Example Notes

This example adds the root element World to the Western hierarchy of the Region dimension. World
is inserted displays immediately before Netherlands in the dimension definition.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchyTopElementInsertDirect('Region', 'Western', 'Netherlands', 'World');
```

### HierarchyUpdateDirect

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:update, category:hierarchy, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:dimension, object:hierarchy, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_hierarchyupdatedirect.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

HierarchyUpdateDirect performs a full rewrite of a hierarchy that has been subject to
direct editing in a TurboIntegrator process, essentially compacting the memory footprint of the
hierarchy.

A dimension that undergoes a series of direct-only edits (element deletions, in particular) will
eventually use more memory than its fully-rewritten counterpart would. This function can optionally
be used after directly editing a dimension with HierarchyElementInsertDirect,
HierarchyElementDeleteDirect, HierarchyElementComponentAddDirect,
HierarchyElementComponentDeleteDirect, and/or HierarchyTopElementInsertDirect. Calling
HierarchyUpdateDirect incurs an initial full-copy memory cost, however it can be used to guarantee
that the dimension is at its smallest possible memory footprint after processing is complete.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
HierarchyUpdateDirect(DimName, HierName);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| DimName | string | The name of the dimension you want to rewrite. |
| HierName | string | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| DimName | The name of the dimension you want to rewrite. |
| HierName | The name of the hierarchy within the dimension. |

#### Example Notes

This example rewrites the Western hierarchy of the Region dimension.

#### Examples

```ti
HierarchyUpdateDirect('Region', 'Western');
```

### TurboIntegrator Functions

- Category: Hierarchy Manipulation TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:hierarchy
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/c_tm1turbointegratorfunctions_n70006.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

TurboIntegrator lets you manipulate
Planning Analytics
data and metadata when you define a
process.

This is accomplished through the use of functions in the Prolog, Metadata, Data, and Epilog
sub-tabs within the Advanced tab of the TurboIntegrator window. These sub-tabs include generated
statements based on settings and options you select when defining a TurboIntegrator process. Any
functions you create must appear after the generated statements. For details on creating processes
with TurboIntegrator, see the
TurboIntegrator
documentation.

- Valid in: unknown

## Logical Rules Functions

### CONTINUE

- Category: Logical Rules Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_continue.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

When included as part of a rules expression, CONTINUE allows a subsequent rule with the
same area definition to be executed. Normally,
Planning Analytics
only executes the first rule encountered for a
given area.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
CONTINUE
```

#### Example Notes

In this example, all cells identified by January and Argentina are assigned a value of 10. Cells
identified by Jan and any other Region element are assigned a value of 20.

#### Examples

```ti
['Jan']= if(!region @= 'Argentina',10,CONTINUE);
```

```ti
['Jan']=20;
```

#### Arguments

None.

### IF

- Category: Logical Rules Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-only
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_if.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

IF returns one value if a logical expression you specify is TRUE and another value if it
is FALSE.

This function is valid in rules only.

TurboIntegrator uses its own IF function that is capable of evaluating multiple logical
expressions.

- Valid in: rule

#### Syntax

```ti
IF(expression, true_value, false_value)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| expression | unknown | Any value or expression that can be evaluated to TRUE or FALSE. |
| true_value | unknown | The value that is returned if expression is TRUE. |
| false_value | unknown | The value that is returned if expression is FALSE. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| expression | Any value or expression that can be evaluated to TRUE or FALSE. |
| true_value | The value that is returned if expression is TRUE. |
| false_value | The value that is returned if expression is FALSE. |

#### Example Notes

IF(1<2, 4, 5) returns 4.

IF(1>2, 'ABC', 'DEF') returns 'DEF'.

### STET

- Category: Logical Rules Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: None
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_stet.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

The STET function cancels the effect of a rule for a particular element.

This is a rules function, valid only in
Planning Analytics
rules. This function cannot be used in
TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: unknown

#### Syntax

```ti
STET
```

#### Example Notes

In this example, the rule dictates that the value for Sales is always 100, except for the
intersection of Sales and the element France from the Region dimension.

#### Examples

```ti
['Sales'] = IF(!Region @= 'France',STET, 100);
```

#### Arguments

None.

### ROUNDP

- Category: Mathematical Rules Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: feature:rules-and-ti, value:number
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_roundp.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ROUNDP rounds a given number at a specified decimal precision.

This function is valid in both rules and TurboIntegrator processes.

- Valid in: both

#### Syntax

```ti
ROUNDP(number, decimal)
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| number | number | The number you want to round. |
| decimal | number | The decimal precision at which to apply the rounding. If this argument is positive, the function
rounds the specified number of digits to the right of the decimal point. If this argument is
negative, the function rounds the specified number of digits to the left of the decimal point. The decimal argument must be between -15 and 15, inclusive. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| number | The number you want to round. |
| decimal | The decimal precision at which to apply the rounding. If this argument is positive, the function
rounds the specified number of digits to the right of the decimal point. If this argument is
negative, the function rounds the specified number of digits to the left of the decimal point. The decimal argument must be between -15 and 15, inclusive. |

#### Example Notes

ROUNDP(1.46, 1) returns 1.5.

ROUNDP(1.466, 2) returns 1.47.

ROUNDP(234.56, -1) returns 230.00.

ROUNDP(234.56, 0) returns 235.00.

## Miscellaneous TurboIntegrator Functions

### ExecuteJavaN

- Category: Miscellaneous TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:execute, category:misc, value:number, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_ti_func_executejavan.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ExecuteJavaN executes a Java™ TurboIntegrator
process that returns a number. If you want to execute a Java
TurboIntegrator process that returns a string, use ExecuteJavaS.

This function is valid in processes only.

This function is not supported in processes on
TM1 Database 12
.

- Valid in: unknown

#### Syntax Variants

```ti
ExecuteJavaN('JavaTIClass', ['OptionalParameter1', 'OptionalParameter2', ...] )
```

```ti
package com.example;

import com.ibm.cognos.tm1.javati.JavaTI;

@JavaTI
public class MyTestTI {
	public static double MyTestTI (String [] args) [
	...
	return ...;
	}
}
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| JavaTIClass | string | The fully qualified name of the Java TurboIntegrator class
you want to execute. |
| OptionalParameters | number | Optional parameters that are passed to the Java
TurboIntegrator process itself. You can pass as many parameters as necessary, including none. You can pass only strings as parameters, you cannot pass numbers. You can use the StringToNumber
TurboIntegrator function to pass numbers to Java
TurboIntegrator scripts. For more information, see "StringToNumber" in the TM1
Reference . |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| JavaTIClass | The fully qualified name of the Java TurboIntegrator class
you want to execute. |
| OptionalParameters | Optional parameters that are passed to the Java
TurboIntegrator process itself. You can pass as many parameters as necessary, including none. You can pass only strings as parameters, you cannot pass numbers. You can use the StringToNumber
TurboIntegrator function to pass numbers to Java
TurboIntegrator scripts. For more information, see "StringToNumber" in the TM1
Reference . |

#### Example Notes

ExecuteJavaN('com.example.MyTestTI', 'First', 'Second', 'Third');

### Expand

- Category: Miscellaneous TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:misc, feature:turbointegrator-only, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_expand.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

Expand expands TurboIntegrator variable names, enclosed in % signs, to their values at
run time. A common use of the Expand function is to pass the value of TurboIntegrator variables to
the ODBCOutput function.

If the variable name represents a string variable, the entire variable expression must be
enclosed on quotes. For example, "%V1%".

If Expand is fed with a numerical value, an implicit type conversion is performed and the
numerical value is converted into a string.

That string has a fixed minimum length of 10 characters. If the converted number is too small to
fill 10 characters, it is padded with leading spaces. Only three leading decimal characters are
converted. For example, a numerical value of 0.123456789 is converted into the string "0.123".

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
Expand(String);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| String | string | Any string that includes TurboIntegrator variable names enclosed in % signs. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| String | Any string that includes TurboIntegrator variable names enclosed in % signs. |

#### Example Notes

This example illustrates the use of the Expand function within the ODBCOutput function. The
example inserts records into a relational table named Sales that consists of three columns: Month,
Product, and Sales.

The Expand function converts the variables V0, V1, and V2 to their actual values within the view.
Assuming that the first value in the view is 123.456, and is defined by the elements Jan and Widget

becomes

at run time.

#### Examples

```ti
ODBCOutPut( 'TransData', Expand( 'INSERT INTO SALES( MONTH, PRODUCT, SALES ) 
VALUES ( "%V0%", "%V1%",%V2% )' ) );
```

```ti
Expand( 'INSERT INTO SALES ( MONTH, PRODUCT, SALES ) VALUES ("%V0%", "%V1%",%V2% )' )
```

```ti
'INSERTINTO SALES ( MONTH, PRODUCT, SALES ) VALUES ( Jan, Widget,123.456 )'
```

### FileExists

- Category: Miscellaneous TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:read, category:misc, feature:explicit-return, feature:turbointegrator-only, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_fileexists.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

FileExists determines whether a specified file exists. The function returns 1 if the file
exists, 0 if it does not.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
FileExists(File);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| File | string | The name of a file. If a full parth is not specified, TM1
searches for the file in the server data directory. |

#### Returns

returns 1 if the file exists, 0 if it does not

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| File | The name of a file. If a full parth is not specified, TM1
searches for the file in the server data directory. |

#### Example Notes

This example determines if the model.dim file exists.

#### Examples

```ti
FileExists('C:\tm1s7\pdata\model.dim');
```

### LogOutput

- Category: Miscellaneous TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-09-03
- Tags: action:export, category:misc, feature:turbointegrator-only, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_logoutput.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

LogOutput writes a message to the
tm1server.log
file
and optionally the process log file
when an error of a specified severity
level is encountered in a TurboIntegrator process.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
LogOutput('SeverityLevel', 'MessageString', 'ProcessLog');
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| SeverityLevel | string | The severity level that initiates logging to the tm1server.log file log files . Valid values
for this argument are: 'DEBUG' 'INFO' 'WARN' 'ERROR' 'FATAL' |
| MessageString | string | The message that you want to write to the tm1server.log file log files . The message
string can be a string that is enclosed in single quotation marks or can be another TurboIntegrator
function that returns a string. |
| ProcessLog | string | Optional. If set to 1, this function also writes the message to the TurboIntegrator process
log file in addition to the tm1server.log file. If set to 0 or not defined,
the function writes messages to just the tm1server.log . |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| SeverityLevel | The severity level that initiates logging to the tm1server.log file log files . Valid values
for this argument are: 'DEBUG' 'INFO' 'WARN' 'ERROR' 'FATAL' |
| MessageString | The message that you want to write to the tm1server.log file log files . The message
string can be a string that is enclosed in single quotation marks or can be another TurboIntegrator
function that returns a string. |
| ProcessLog | Optional. If set to 1, this function also writes the message to the TurboIntegrator process
log file in addition to the tm1server.log file. If set to 0 or not defined,
the function writes messages to just the tm1server.log . |

#### Examples

```ti
LogOutput('WARN', 'TI process encountered a warning condition');
```

```ti
LogOutput('ERROR', TM1User(), 0);
```

```ti
LogOutput('INFO', 'TI process execution finished normally', 1);
```

#### Prerequisite

To enable message logging from TurboIntegrator, you must add the
TM1.TILogOutput
debugger to the
tm1-log.properties
file and set the debugger to the wanted level.
For example, adding
TM1.TILogOutput=DEBUG
to
tm1-log.properties
enables logging for all severity levels. For more
information on the
tm1-log.properties
file, see
“
Configuring and Enabling
Server Message Logging
”
in
TM1 Operations
.

### TM1User

- Category: Miscellaneous TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:misc, feature:turbointegrator-only
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_id_miscellaneousturbointegratorfunctions_n72f55_5120tm1user.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

TM1User returns a string giving the current TM1®
client. When executed in a process that the user is running directly, it will return the user's TM1 client name. When executed in a chore that the user runs
directly, it will also return the user's TM1 client name.

If run from a scheduled chore, it will return a name in the form
R*<chore name>
, for
example,
R*UpdateRegionDimension
.

This function is valid in TM1 TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
TM1User()
```

### TurboIntegrator Functions

- Category: Miscellaneous TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:misc
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/c_tm1turbointegratorfunctions_n70006.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

TurboIntegrator lets you manipulate
Planning Analytics
data and metadata when you define a
process.

This is accomplished through the use of functions in the Prolog, Metadata, Data, and Epilog
sub-tabs within the Advanced tab of the TurboIntegrator window. These sub-tabs include generated
statements based on settings and options you select when defining a TurboIntegrator process. Any
functions you create must appear after the generated statements. For details on creating processes
with TurboIntegrator, see the
TurboIntegrator
documentation.

- Valid in: unknown

### WildcardFileSearch

- Category: Miscellaneous TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: category:misc, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:file, value:string
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_wildcardfilesearch.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

WildcardFileSearch lets you use wildcard characters to search for files in a specified
directory.

The results of the WildCardFileSearch function may vary depending on the operating system in use.
Files in a Windows directory are sorted in alphabetical
order while files in a UNIX directory are sorted in random
order. Because the order of sorting varies between the operating systems, the identical
WildCardFileSearch function executed against identical directories, one on Windows and one on UNIX, will yield
different results.

This function is valid in TM1® TurboIntegrator processes
only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
WildcardFileSearch( Pathname, PriorFilename);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Pathname | string | A pathname to files for which you want to search. The pathname must end in a filename, which can
contain a wildcard sequence using the * and/or ? characters. The ? wildcard character matches any single character. The * wildcard character matches zero or more characters. |
| PriorFilename | string | The name of an existing file in the specified directory. This filename cannot contain wildcard
characters. The wildcard search specified by the Pathname argument will commence AFTER this
file. If you pass an empty string as the PriorFilename argument, the WildcardFileSearch function
returns the first file that matches the wildcard sequence specified by the Pathname argument. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| Pathname | A pathname to files for which you want to search. The pathname must end in a filename, which can
contain a wildcard sequence using the * and/or ? characters. The ? wildcard character matches any single character. The * wildcard character matches zero or more characters. |
| PriorFilename | The name of an existing file in the specified directory. This filename cannot contain wildcard
characters. The wildcard search specified by the Pathname argument will commence AFTER this
file. If you pass an empty string as the PriorFilename argument, the WildcardFileSearch function
returns the first file that matches the wildcard sequence specified by the Pathname argument. |

#### Example Notes

The following example shows the use of the WildcardFileSearch function to determine the first
server log file generated in 2004:

This example returns the first file matching the wildcard sequence 'tm1s2004*.log' from the
C:\Program Files\Cognos\TM1\Custom\TM1Data\SData\ directory.

Because server log files are named and saved with sequential time stamps, and because the second
parameter to WildcardFileSearch is empty, the function returns the first server log file starting
with the characters 'tm1s2004'. This would be the first server log file generated in the year
2004.

The following example shows the use of the WildcardFileSearch function to return the first server
log file generated after tm1s20040211153827.log was generated:

This example begins searching the C:\Program Files\Cognos\TM1\Custom\TM1Data\SData\ directory
immediately after the tm1s20040211153827.log file, and returns the first subsequent file matching
the 'tm1s*.log' wildcard sequence.

tm1s20040220175522.log is the first file that occurs after tm1s20040211153827.log and matches the
wildcard sequence. Accordingly, the example returns tm1s20040220175522.log.

#### Examples

```ti
file = WildcardFileSearch( 'C:\Program Files\Cognos\TM1\Custom\
TM1Data\SData\tm1s2004*.log', ' ');
```

```ti
file = WildcardFileSearch( 'C:\Program Files\Cognos\TM1\Custom\
TM1Data\SData\tm1s*.log', 'tm1s20040211153827.log
');
```

### ODBCOPENEx

- Category: ODBC TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19

- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_id_odbcturbointegratorfunctions_n719eb_1926odbcopenex.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

opened as a Unicode connection.

only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

```ti
ODBCOpenEx(Source, ClientName, Password, UseUnicodeODBC);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |


```ti
chinese= ;
chinese = CHARW( 37123 );
fieldval = chinese | SomeNewText;
sql= Update TestTable set ForeName = N | fieldval |  WHERE CustomerId= 1
ODBCOUTPUT( Unicode, sql );
```

```ti
Update TestTable set ForeName = N?SomeNewText WHERE
CustomerId = 1
```

### ODBCOutput

- Category: ODBC TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:export, category:odbc, feature:turbointegrator-only, object:odbc
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_tm1_ref_tifun_odbcoutput.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

ODBCOutput executes an SQL update query against an open ODBC data source. You should use
the ODBCOpen function to open the data source before calling ODBCOutput, and use ODBCClose to close
the data source before exiting the process.

This function is valid in TurboIntegrator processes only.

- Valid in: turbointegrator

#### Syntax

```ti
ODBCOutput(Source, SQLQuery, [SQLQuery2, SQLQuery3, ...]);
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Source | unknown | The ODBC data source against which you want to run a query. |
| SQLQuery | unknown | An SQL query statement. Though ODBCOutput was developed to update tables, it can be used to execute any SQL query on the
data source. In circumstances where the SQL query statement exceeds 255 characters, you should split the query
into multiple SQLQuery arguments (SQLQuery2, SQLQuery3, etc.). This lets you create query statements
that exceed the 255 character limit for TurboIntegrator arguments. When the ODBCOutput function is
executed, all SQLQuery arguments are concatenated and the query is successfully executed. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| Source | The ODBC data source against which you want to run a query. |
| SQLQuery | An SQL query statement. Though ODBCOutput was developed to update tables, it can be used to execute any SQL query on the
data source. In circumstances where the SQL query statement exceeds 255 characters, you should split the query
into multiple SQLQuery arguments (SQLQuery2, SQLQuery3, etc.). This lets you create query statements
that exceed the 255 character limit for TurboIntegrator arguments. When the ODBCOutput function is
executed, all SQLQuery arguments are concatenated and the query is successfully executed. |

#### Example Notes

This example executes the specified query against the Accounting data source.

#### Examples

```ti
ODBCOutput('Accounting', 'INSERT [CategoryID], [CategoryName]FROM Categories;');
```

### SetODBCUnicodeInterface

- Category: ODBC TurboIntegrator Functions
- Last updated: 2025-03-19
- Tags: action:update, category:odbc, object:odbc
- Source: https://www.ibm.com/docs/api/v1/content/SSD29G_2.0.0/com.ibm.swg.ba.cognos.tm1_ref.2.0.0.doc/r_id_odbcturbointegratorfunctions_n719eb_2024setodbcunicodeinterface.html?parsebody=true&lang=en

#### Description

SetODBCUnicodeInterface sets whether the ODBC interface should use the Unicode wide
functions or the regular single-byte character functions. Setting this function to 1 uses the wide
character ODBC interface.

Some ODBC driver support either the older single-byte interface as well as a Unicode style
'wide-character' interface, where characters are passed and retrieved as 16-bit quantities. If the
driver chosen does not support one or the other style, a flag is provided to force TurboIntegrator
to use a particular style of interface.

This function is valid in processes only.

This function is not supported in processes on
TM1 Database 12
.

- Valid in: unknown

#### Syntax

```ti
SetODBCUnicodeInterface=1
```

#### Parameters

| Name | Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | unknown | Use the wide character ODBC interface. |
| 0 | unknown | Use the single-byte interface. |

#### Arguments

| Argument | Description |
| --- | --- |
| 1 | Use the wide character ODBC interface. |
| 0 | Use the single-byte interface. |
